# Text Elements
Neural Networks ^Db1ujiiW

What is a neural network? ^voYqYfOm

Inspired by humans, Neural networks mimic the neuron system in our body,
consisting of many simple neurons that trigger certain results given certain stimuli
working all together to recognize a pattern and adapting itself to produce an appropriate result ^nUamIlf6

How does an artificial neuron look like? ^cKBeYcMg

ai ^aqoQ7fhq

wij ^acRhqtp7

bj ^BzaBExpx

ai+2 ^cvvB1G3s

ai+3 ^Wrir944H

g(x) ^N5sW6fle

aj ^XU7mSWbO

Has the ability to adjust
and learn with weights ^c5LRvggw

has the ability to
produce nonlinear
representations depending
on the function ^eMfWkYgG

includes prior information ^Novfee8e

xi ^aWZMkAL8

xi+1 ^jTVtORhp

xi+2 ^iLILoIxA

Why neural networks? ^8p0LfI15

To understand this we need to understand three key concepts about models ^m1PvggVB

Universality ^iwj58cIT

Compactness ^sSRkSGSh

Optimization ^AYU1CEBY

Can they approximate any functions
(assuming we have enough neurons)? ^QZRZlzmd

With sufficiently many neurons, neural networks can
approximate any nonlinear functions ^o7XbR7xF

Any function y(x1,x2) such that x1 is constant and x2 is variable
can be approximated as an infinite fourier series ^rs6392VD

Similarly the coefficients themselves can be approximated using the same method ^SAlIuGy8

Using the cosine multiplication identity ^Zj0MXvkM

This is a two-layer neural network, except for the cosine nonlinearity.
The latter can however be approximated by a superposition of a large
number of step functions ^KfpykY80

Neural networks can express a broad range of `useful'
functions in compact manner ^pkICLuwu

The neural network starts
with a finite and typically
small set of randomly
initialized neurons (i.e. a
subset of all possible
neurons ^uiDIXxaa

The learned representation is
almost as predictive as an
exhaustive set of neurons,
but much more compact ^XRlkLTb9

Neural networks also have downsides ^zQGZViTJ

Multiple layers can cause pathological
curvature, i.e. the gradient vanishes
along certain directions of the parameter
space. The optimizer may get stuck on
large plateaus ^yAMlmnWE

BUT ^Y1cdPzHN

With heuristics on the neural network de-sign
and optimization, it is however still possible to
train them efficiently. ^SSihdbW9

How do we train a multi-layer neural network? ^08N8BcCu

forward pass ^LjYoG3An

Perceptron ^FPBSdU1v

let xi be a collection of datapoints such that they belong to label t
the goal of the perceptron is to correctly seperate all available points into different groups
y = t
such that 
y = sign(wx+b) ^hAeLtVnc

the perceptron algorithm is quite simple
start with a random initialization and iterate N times
if your model correctly classifies that point, do nothing
else adjust your weight and bias with xt * learning_rate
only stop once all datapoints are correctly classified ^TdBJu2Dt

The perceptron objective can be seen as a gradient descent of the error function ^ebPD9b5T

Just like we formulated the perceptron objective into the gradient descent, we can generalize
this to an entire neural network compromised of different perceptron neurons
and the error function is the error of the output of the entire network ^7So9JEJB

The backwards pass ^plxwgE9k

In order to compute the backwards pass method to find the gradient of the error function
we need to use the chain derivative rule and generalize it for an entire network ^aacJQilB

Chain Derivative rule for one path (Univariate) ^kesbt24a

The derivative of z w.r.t to a parameter theta is the chainrule
of derivatives of the path taken from theta to z ^OLv29Puw

What if there were
multiple paths? ^mWuOmA4G

Chain derivatives rule for multiple paths (Multivariate) ^8v0fV6Rt

The derivative of z w.r.t to a parameter theta is the chainrule
of derivatives given every single possible path from theta to z ^IhBqmyAX

This can grow very large with increasingly more layers and neurons ^I4ZAluzB

This can be rewritten in a way that avoids
redundant computation, turning it into a linear
complexity algorithm ^6FDbfEfb

Error back-propagation ^OoVCoBWW

Where delta is the gradient given at a certain neuron given all paths that go to it
and can be re-useable for the entire layer without the need to re-compute
this method is computed from the output to the input ^Ij7ndBuf

Neural Network Example ^V0JHPi7m

Gradient at
neuron j ^swqiqCPI

iterate over all
neurons in the
layer after it ^5yVKygq7

calculate the
gradient at their
level ^jJ6Iudwi

the gradient of
the function
of the neuron
at k after being
passed parameters
from j
using
f(g(x) = f'(g(x) * g'(x) ^uwSRjN9v

a similar thing can be calculated for
the weight except the weights are not interconnected
via multiple connections therefore the sum is not needed ^eh8Vh6eA

Formulated Layer by Layer ^xzr3bIiq

Layer by Layer but for weights ^7EljbU5A

element-wise
multiplication ^EqngGOIv

choice of activation functions ^64oAPItU

for this to apply we need to choose an activation function for the neurons such that we
know how to differentiate it or find it derivative i.e non-zero and defined everywhere
and informative of the increase and decrease of the function ^jbF881vO

ReLu ^Cbm6y5YK

hyperbolic tan ^94RHf52J

softmax ^3oN2XQXH

More about those later! ^SqbCHzEM

What if the parameters we use are shared? ^jAaVS5QN

Some neural networks are built in a way such that the weights going
from one neuron to another is shared with multiple other neurons
such that if one of them updates it, all of them receive the same update ^aUA9jxHW

Shared parameters can be handled by treating original parameters as "neurons"
generated from the new parameters, and appling the chain rule one step further ^b2GRYLLf

Z7 ^bXpTcYg1

a5 ^pOyWUXSl

u ^BJDUAKgz

Z7 ^c6KOFxEa

u ^lEfCGjXj

w13 ^TFcedUjT

w24 ^7yDt8zOa

w36 ^DldLkxUQ

w57 ^ygVtSN94

path from w13 to z7 ^7Gr0cHnc

path from w24 to z7 ^KciRvI48

path from w36 to z7 ^aun2LgtZ

path from w57 to z7 ^FR7yVbDG

What is Gradient descent? ^19ugwy1h

It implies that any suitably smooth function can be approximated
with any precision using neural networks ^djOYpWAU
